<p><b>Christianity</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[note 1]</a></sup> is an <a href="/wiki/Abrahamic_religions" title="Abrahamic religions">Abrahamic</a> <a href="/wiki/Monotheism" title="Monotheism">monotheistic</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Monotheism_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Monotheism-2">[1]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Religion" title="Religion">religion</a> based on the <a href="/wiki/Life_of_Jesus_in_the_New_Testament" title="Life of Jesus in the New Testament">life</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Jesus" title="Ministry of Jesus">teachings</a> of <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">Jesus Christ</a>, who is the <a href="/wiki/Jesus_in_Christianity" title="Jesus in Christianity">focal point of the Christian faith</a>. It is the <a href="/wiki/Major_religious_groups#Largest_religions" title="Major religious groups">world's largest religion</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PewDec2012_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-PewDec2012-4">[3]</a></sup> with over 2.4 billion followers,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-World-5">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gordonconwell.edu_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-gordonconwell.edu-6">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Global_Christianity_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Global_Christianity-7">[6]</a></sup> or 33% of the global population, known as <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">Christians</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-name_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-name-8">[note 2]</a></sup> Christians make up a majority of the population in <a href="/wiki/Christianity_by_country" title="Christianity by country">158 countries and territories</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Global_Christianity_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Global_Christianity-7">[6]</a></sup> They believe that Jesus is the <a href="/wiki/Son_of_God_(Christianity)" title="Son of God (Christianity)">Son of God</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Salvation_in_Christianity" title="Salvation in Christianity">savior of humanity</a> whose coming as the <a href="/wiki/Messiah" title="Messiah">Messiah</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Christ_(title)" title="Christ (title)">Christ</a>) was prophesied in the <a href="/wiki/Old_Testament" title="Old Testament">Old Testament</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[7]</a></sup> Christianity has played a <a href="/wiki/Role_of_Christianity_in_civilization" title="Role of Christianity in civilization">prominent role</a> in the shaping of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_civilization" title="Western civilization">Western civilization</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cambridge_University_Historical_Series_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cambridge_University_Historical_Series-11">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Caltron_J.H_Hayas_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Caltron_J.H_Hayas-12">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Horst_Hutter_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Horst_Hutter-13">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fred_Reinhard_Dallmayr_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fred_Reinhard_Dallmayr-14">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>Christianity grew out of <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Benko1984_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Benko1984-15">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bergen2000_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bergen2000-16">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cory2015_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cory2015-17">[15]</a></sup> and began as a <a href="/wiki/Second_Temple_Judaism" title="Second Temple Judaism">Second Temple Judaic</a> sect in the mid-1st century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Robinson_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Robinson-18">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Esler_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Esler-19">[17]</a></sup> Originating in the <a href="/wiki/Roman_province" title="Roman province">Roman province</a> of <a href="/wiki/Judea_(Roman_province)" title="Judea (Roman province)">Judea</a>, it <a href="/wiki/Early_centers_of_Christianity" title="Early centers of Christianity">quickly spread</a> to <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syria_(region)" title="Syria (region)">Syria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Asia Minor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Transcaucasia" title="Transcaucasia">Transcaucasia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>, and by the end of the 4th century had become the official <a href="/wiki/State_church_of_the_Roman_Empire" title="State church of the Roman Empire">state church of the Roman Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[20]</a></sup> Following the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a>, Christianity spread to the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">sub-Saharan Africa</a> and the rest of the world through <a href="/wiki/Christian_mission" title="Christian mission">missionary work</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_colonialism" title="History of colonialism">colonization</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spread_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Spread-23">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charity_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Charity-24">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Service_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Service-25">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Christian_theology" title="Christian theology">Christian theology</a> is summarized in creeds such as the <a href="/wiki/Apostles%27_Creed" title="Apostles' Creed">Apostles' Creed</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Nicene_Creed" title="Nicene Creed">Nicene Creed</a>. These <a href="/wiki/Profession_(religious)" title="Profession (religious)">professions</a> of faith state that Jesus <a href="/wiki/Passion_of_Jesus" title="Passion of Jesus">suffered</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crucifixion_of_Jesus" title="Crucifixion of Jesus">died</a>, was <a href="/wiki/Burial_of_Jesus" title="Burial of Jesus">buried</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harrowing_of_Hell" title="Harrowing of Hell">descended into hell</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Resurrection_of_Jesus" title="Resurrection of Jesus">rose</a> from the dead, in order to grant <a href="/wiki/Eternal_life_(Christianity)" title="Eternal life (Christianity)">eternal life</a> to those who believe in him and trust in him for the <a href="/wiki/Forgiveness#Christianity" title="Forgiveness">remission</a> of their <a href="/wiki/Christian_views_on_sin" title="Christian views on sin">sins</a>. The creeds further maintain that Jesus physically <a href="/wiki/Ascension_of_Jesus" title="Ascension of Jesus">ascended</a> into <a href="/wiki/Heaven_in_Christianity" title="Heaven in Christianity">heaven</a>, where he reigns with <a href="/wiki/God_the_Father" title="God the Father">God the Father</a> in the unity of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Spirit_in_Christianity" title="Holy Spirit in Christianity">Holy Spirit</a>, and that he will <a href="/wiki/Second_Coming" title="Second Coming">return</a> to <a href="/wiki/Last_Judgment" title="Last Judgment">judge</a> the living and the dead and grant <a href="/wiki/Eternal_life_(Christianity)" title="Eternal life (Christianity)">eternal life</a> to his followers. His <a href="/wiki/Incarnation_(Christianity)" title="Incarnation (Christianity)">incarnation</a>, earthly ministry, <a href="/wiki/Crucifixion_of_Jesus" title="Crucifixion of Jesus">crucifixion</a> and resurrection are often referred to as "<a href="/wiki/The_gospel" title="The gospel">the gospel</a>", meaning "good news".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[note 3]</a></sup> The term <i><a href="/wiki/Gospel" title="Gospel">gospel</a></i> also refers to written accounts of Jesus' life and teaching, four of which—<a href="/wiki/Gospel_of_Matthew" title="Gospel of Matthew">Matthew</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gospel_of_Mark" title="Gospel of Mark">Mark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gospel_of_Luke" title="Gospel of Luke">Luke</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gospel_of_John" title="Gospel of John">John</a>—are considered <a href="/wiki/Biblical_canon" title="Biblical canon">canonical</a> and included in the Christian <a href="/wiki/Bible" title="Bible">Bible</a>, as <a href="/wiki/Development_of_the_Christian_biblical_canon" title="Development of the Christian biblical canon">established</a> by the 5th century<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[24]</a></sup> for the ancient undivided <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox</a> traditions before the <a href="/wiki/East%E2%80%93West_Schism" title="East–West Schism">East–West Schism</a>.</p>
<p>Throughout <a href="/wiki/History_of_Christianity" title="History of Christianity">its history</a>, Christianity has weathered <a href="/wiki/Schism" title="Schism">schisms</a> and theological disputes that have resulted in many distinct churches and <a href="/wiki/Christian_denomination" title="Christian denomination">denominations</a>. Worldwide, the largest branches of Christianity are the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oriental_Orthodoxy" title="Oriental Orthodoxy">Oriental Orthodoxy</a>, as well as thousands of denominations and congregations of <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a>, the latter due to fundamentally different <a href="/wiki/Protestant_ecclesiology" title="Protestant ecclesiology">ecclesiology</a>. The Catholic and Eastern Orthodox churches broke <a href="/wiki/Communion_(religion)" title="Communion (religion)">communion</a> with each other in the <a href="/wiki/East%E2%80%93West_Schism" title="East–West Schism">East–West Schism</a> of 1054. Protestantism came into existence in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" title="Protestant Reformation">Protestant Reformation</a> in the 16th century, splitting from the Catholic Church.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[25]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Beliefs">Beliefs</span></h2>
<p>There are many important differences of interpretation and opinion of the <a href="/wiki/Bible" title="Bible">Bible</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sacred_tradition" title="Sacred tradition">sacred tradition</a> on which Christianity is based.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Olsen_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Olsen-29">[26]</a></sup> Because of these irreconcilable differences in theology and a lack of consensus on the core tenets of Christianity, <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestants</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Orthodox</a> often deny that members of certain other branches are Christians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[27]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Creeds">Creeds</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Creed#Christian_creeds" title="Creed">Creed § Christian creeds</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Christian_creeds" title="List of Christian creeds">List of Christian creeds</a></div>
<table class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" role="presentation" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="430" data-file-width="410" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/38px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/57px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/76px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png 2x" width="38"/></td>
